Partnership of Craftsmen: Validity by Istihsan
Inter-madhhab dispute on partnership based on work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits Shirkat al-Taqabbul and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by citing the key proofs.

Core Idea
A partnership based solely on work is valid because profit can arise from work, not just capital.

This passage addresses a core Hanafi concession: the permissibility of partnership among craftsmen who pool their labor, not capital. While other schools require capital contribution, the Hanafi school, using istihsan, validates such arrangements. We will explore the arguments and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What exactly is being contested? The permissibility of a partnership where no capital is contributed—only work (shirkat al-taqabbul).
Also called shirkat al-abdan or shirkat al-sana'i'.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school (Imam Muhammad) says it is ja'iz (permissible) by istihsan. The proof: profit is not limited to capital; work generates profit. Each partner acts as principal and agent, creating a valid agency that leads to shared profit.
The text says 'ولنا أن المقصود منهما...'
3
State the opposing position and proof
Al-Shafi'i, Zafar (in one narration), and Malik say it is invalid. Their proof: partnership in profit requires partnership in capital (ra's al-mal). Without capital, profit cannot be imagined.
They argue the foundation of profit is capital.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the objective of the partners is to acquire profit jointly, and this is achieved through work. The contract of agency (tawkeel) is valid; each is a principal in his own work and an agent in the other's. This realizes partnership in the resulting property (the fee).
Also, 'هذا العقد مما يقبل التوكيل فيجوز'
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis allow two tailors or a tailor and a dyer to partner without capital; Shafi'is require each to contribute capital. This affects many small craftsmen and service providers.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقبل إن اشترك خياطان أو خياط وصباغ على أن يتقبلا الأعمال ويكون الكسب بينهما، وكل عمل يتقبله أحدهما بينهما، وكذا بين الشريكين على الانفراد، وقيد بما ذكر للاحتراز عن الشركة فالشريك لا يشارك؛ لأن الشيء لا يتضمن مثله، الوكيل ليس له التوكيل والمضارب ليس له أن يضارب؛ لما قلنا: إن الشيء لا يستتبع المثل، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه ليس له المضاربة؛ لأنه نوع شركة، والأصح ما ذكر، وهو رواية الأصل. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) ويوكل: أجنبيا ببيع وشراء؛ لأنه متعارف بينهم. (ط، عيني) ويده في المال إلخ لأنه قبضه بإذن صاحبه لا على وجه المبادلة والوثيقة، فصار كالوديعة والعارية بخلاف المقبوض على سوم الشراء؛ لأنه مقبوض على وجه البدل، وبخلاف المقبوض على الرهن؛ لأنه مقبوض على وجه الوثيقة والحاصل أن المال في يد كل واحد من الشريكين أمانة كالوديعة والعارية فيقبل قوله بيمينه في مقدار الربح والخسران والضياع والدفع لشريكه، ولو ادعاه بعد موته، لا يضمن إلا بالتعدي ومثله المضارب والوصي والمتولي. (مستخلص، فتح) وتقبل: [ أي الثالث من أنواع شركة العقد شركة تقبل، وتسمى شركة الصنائع وشركة الأعمال أيضاً. (عيني) ] وتسمى شركة الأبدان أيضاً، وهي أن يشترك صانعان أن يتقبلا العمل، ويكون الكسب بينهما، سواء كانا متحدي العمل كالخياطين أو مختلفي العمل كخياط وصباغ بلا اختلاط مال وهي جائزة عندنا، وقال الشافعي وزفر في رواية: لا يجوز؛ لأن الشركة في الربح تبتني على الشركة في رأس المال، ولا مال لهما، فكيف يتصور الربح بدون الأصل؟ ولنا أن المقصود منهما إنما هو تحصيل الربح على الاشتراك، وهو لا يقتصر على المال بل يكون بالعمل أيضاً، فإذا وكل كل منهما الآخر بقبول العمل، كان كل واحد أصلاً في نصف العمل المتقبل، ووكيلاً في النصف الآخر، فتحقق الشركة في المال المستفاد وهو الربح، وهذا العقد مما يقبل التوكيل فيجوز. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني وصباغ أو نحوهما فلا يلزم اتحاد صنعة ومكان. ويكون الكسب بينهما أي أجر الكسب الذي يمكن استحقاقه كتعليم كتابة وقرآن وفقه على المفتى به، بخلاف شركة دلالين ومفتيين وشهود محاكم وقراء ووعاظ وسؤال؛ لأن التوكيل بالسؤال لا يصح، وكذا لواشتركا في عمل حرام لم يصح، وأما شركة الحمالين فصحيحة، فالأجر الذي يحصل من العمل يكون بين الشريكين مناصفة، ولو شرطا أكثر الربح لأدناهما عملا فالأصح الجواز، وكون الكسب بينهما يجوز استحساناً عندنا، وقال زفر ومالك: لا يجوز مع اختلاف الصنعة والمكان كالخياط والصباغ؛ لأن الشركة هي الخلطة، ولا خلطة فيها. ولنا: أن أول هذا العقد توكيل بالتصرف، وآخره اشتراك في الربح، فصار كالمضاربة، فلا يشترط اتحاد الصنعة، وكذا لا يشترط اتحاد المكان مثل أن يُجلس آخر على دكانه فيطرح عليه العمل بالنصف، والقياس أن - الصنعة،
And accepting work (taqabbul): if two tailors, or a tailor and a dyer, join together on the condition that they accept work and the earnings be between them, and every work accepted by one of them is between them, and likewise between the two partners individually. And he restricted (the ruling) to what was mentioned to avoid (confusion with) partnership: because a partner does not participate (in a similar partnership), for a thing does not include its like; the agent (wakil) does not have the right to appoint an agent, and the mudarib does not have the right to enter into mudaraba, because we said: a thing does not entail its like. And from Abu Hanifa it is reported that he (the mudarib) does not have the right to mudaraba, because it is a type of partnership. And the most correct is what we mentioned, and it is the riwayah of the origin. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) And he appoints a wakil: a third party for buying and selling, because it is customary among them. (Ta, Ayni) And his hand over the property (is a trust) etc. because he took possession with the permission of his owner, not on the basis of exchange or security, so it becomes like a deposit (wadi'a) and a loan for use (i'arah), unlike what is taken on the basis of a purchase negotiation (sawm al-shira'), because it is taken on the basis of exchange, and unlike what is taken as collateral (rahn), because it is taken on the basis of security. And the conclusion: that the property in the hand of each of the two partners is a trust like a deposit and loan for use, so his statement (regarding the amount of profit, loss, wastage, and payment to his partner) is accepted upon his oath. If he claims it after his death, he is not liable except for transgression. And similarly the mudarib, executor (wasi), and administrator (mutawalli). (Mustakhlas, Fath) And accepting work (taqabbul): [i.e., the third type of contract partnership is partnership of acceptance (shirkat taqabbul), and it is also called partnership of crafts (shirkat al-sana'i') and partnership of works (shirkat al-a'mal). (Ayni)] And it is also called partnership of bodies (shirkat al-abdan), and it is that two craftsmen join together to accept work, and the earnings be between them, whether they are united in craft like two tailors, or different in craft like a tailor and a dyer, without mixing of capital. And it is permissible (ja'iz) in our (Hanafi) school. And al-Shafi'i and Zafar (in one narration) said: it is not permissible, because partnership in profit is built upon partnership in capital, and they have no capital, so how can profit be imagined without principal? And our proof: what is intended by them is only to acquire profit jointly, and this is not limited to capital but also occurs through work. So if each of them appoints the other as agent to accept work, then each is a principal in half of the work accepted and an agent in the other half, thus partnership is realized in the resulting property, which is profit. And this contract is one that accepts agency, so it is valid. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) And a dyer or the like: thus unity of craft and place are not required. And the earnings are between them: meaning the fee for earning that can be claimed, such as teaching writing, Quran, and fiqh, according to the mufta bihi. Unlike the partnership of brokers (dallalin), muftis, court witnesses, Quran reciters, preachers, and beggars, because agency for begging is not valid. Similarly, if they partner in a prohibited work, it is not valid. As for the partnership of porters (hammalin), it is valid, so the fee obtained from the work is between the partners equally. If they stipulate more profit for the one who does less work, the most correct is that it is permissible. And that the earnings be between them is permissible by istihsan in our school. And Zafar and Malik said: it is not permissible with difference of craft and place, like the tailor and dyer, because partnership is mixing (khalta), and there is no mixing. And our proof: the beginning of this contract is agency to act, and its end is sharing in profit, so it becomes like mudaraba; thus unity of craft is not required, and similarly unity of place is not required, such as that one sits another on his shop and assigns work to him for half. And by qiyas - the craft... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage discusses Shirkat al-Taqabbul (partnership of acceptance), also known as Shirkat al-Abdan or Shirkat al-Sana'i'. It is a partnership based on work rather than capital, where two craftsmen agree to jointly accept work and share earnings. The commentator first addresses some ancillary issues: a partner cannot engage in a separate similar partnership because a thing does not include its like; similarly, an agent cannot appoint another agent, and a mudarib cannot enter another mudaraba, as per a narration from Abu Hanifa. Then the main discussion begins: the definition and permissibility. Imam Muhammad (and the Hanafi school) deem it valid, while al-Shafi'i and Zafar hold it invalid because profit-sharing requires capital. The Hanafi response is that the objective is profit, achievable through work as well; each partner acts as principal and agent, creating a valid agency-based partnership. The passage then lists examples: tailors, dyers, porters, teachers of writing, Quran, and fiqh are permissible, but partnerships of brokers, muftis, court witnesses, Quran reciters, preachers, and beggars are invalid because agency for begging is invalid or the work is not permissible. The text also addresses the condition of unity of craft and place: the Hanafi school does not require them, citing istihsan. Zafar and Malik require unity. The passage ends mid-sentence, suggesting the original text continues.

Key Terms
شَرِكَة التَقَبُّل (shirkat al-taqabbul): Partnership of acceptance: craftsmen agree to jointly accept work and share fees.
شَرِكَة الأَبْدَان (shirkat al-abdan): Same as shirkat al-taqabbul; emphasizes partnership based on physical work.
اسْتِحْسَان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding strict qiyas; used here to validate the partnership despite lack of capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is the partnership of a tailor and a dyer (different crafts) valid?
A) No, because their crafts are different
B) Yes, by istihsan, unity of craft is not required
C) Only if they also contribute capital
D) No, because a partnership of bodies requires identical work

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-Taqabbul is a valid Hanafi partnership based on work, permissible by istihsan even without capital, and without requiring identical crafts or place.

Shirkah — Partnership

Partner's Authority to Enter into Mudaraba: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudaraba by partner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on a partner entering into a mudaraba, identify Abu Hanifa's opposing view, and explain the tarjih mechanism based on the principle 'al-shay' la yastatba' mithlahu'.

Core Idea
A partner may enter into mudaraba with partnership capital; Abu Hanifa's objection is overruled by the Sahibayn and custom.

The passage begins by listing the partner's general authorities: to hire, deposit, enter into mudaraba, and appoint agents. However, a critical intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding mudaraba. Abu Hanifa held that a partner cannot enter into a mudaraba because mudaraba itself is a type of partnership, and a thing does not entail its like. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagreed, and their view, supported by istihsan and customary practice, became the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the tarjih process that settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Partner's General Authorities
The text states that a partner may hire workers, deposit funds, enter into mudaraba, and appoint an agent. Note that these are default permissions unless explicitly restricted.
These are permissive acts, not fard or wajib.
2
Highlight the Disputed Act: Mudaraba
The text then restricts the general rule by quoting Abu Hanifa's objection: the partner cannot enter into a mudaraba with the partnership capital. This is the point of contention.
The dispute is only about mudaraba, not about hiring or depositing.
3
Understand the Opposing Dalil: Al-Shay' La Yastatba' Mithlahu
Abu Hanifa's proof is the principle that a thing does not entail its like. Since mudaraba is a type of partnership, a partner cannot create another partnership from the same capital, as this would lead to infinite regress.
This is a rational argument (dalil aqli).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
The Sahibayn respond that mudaraba is a separate agency contract, and the partner acts as an agent of the partnership. Custom (urf) permits it. The text declares the Sahibayn's view as al-ashah (the correct) and riwayat al-asl (the transmission of the original), making it mufta bihi.
The tarjih is based on both textual transmission (zahir al-riwayah) and practical custom (istihsan).
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Under Abu Hanifa's view, if the partner enters into a mudaraba, the contract is invalid and profits belong to the original partnership. Under the relied-upon view, the mudaraba is valid and profits are distributed as agreed.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And he may hire, deposit, enter into mudaraba, and appoint an agent, and his hand over the capital is a trust. Meaning: by giving the capital as mudaraba. And it is valid if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer associate on condition that they accept work and the earnings (and every work that either of them accepts) are between them, and between the two partners. And it is restricted by what was mentioned to exclude partnership, for a partner does not enter into a partnership with his partner because a thing does not include its like; an agent does not have the right to delegate, and a mudarib does not have the right to enter into a mudaraba because we said that a thing does not entail its like. Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from the matn regarding the powers of a partner in a partnership and the legal status of the capital in his hands. The text first states that a partner may hire workers, deposit funds, enter into a mudaraba, and appoint an agent, but then it clarifies that the partner cannot become a mudarib with the partnership capital according to Abu Hanifa, because mudaraba is itself a type of partnership and a partner cannot create another partnership with the same capital. However, the relied-upon position (al-ashah) and the narration of the original (riwayat al-asl) allow it. This is based on the principle that a thing does not entail its like (al-shay' la yastatba' mithlahu). The passage then explains that the partner's hand over the capital is a trust (amanah), similar to wadi'ah deposit and ariyah loan, because he took possession with permission but not as an exchange or security. Unlike a buyer who takes goods on approval (sawm al-shira') where possession is for substitution, or a pledge where possession is for security, the partner's possession is purely permissive and thus trust. Consequently, the partner's statement under oath is accepted regarding profit, loss, destruction, and payment to his co-partner. Even if a partner claims after his death, he is not liable unless he committed transgression. The same rule applies to the mudarib, executor, and administrator of a waqf.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudaraba): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit sharing agreed upon. In this dispute, it is considered a separate agency contract by the Sahibayn.
الشيء لا يستتبع مثله (al-shay' la yastatba' mithlahu): A principle meaning 'a thing does not entail its like'. Used by Abu Hanifa to argue that a partnership cannot create another partnership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because a thing cannot entail its like.
B) Yes, because it is customary and considered valid by istihsan.
C) No, only if the other partner agrees in writing.
D) Yes, but the other partner must be the mudarib.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows a partner to enter into a mudaraba with partnership capital, overriding Abu Hanifa's objection through istihsan and custom.

Shirkah — Partnership

Capital in Partnership as a Trust: Amanah Rules and Evidentiary Implications
Explains the amanah nature of partnership capital and its legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why partnership capital is treated as a trust (amanah) and identify the evidentiary rule that the partner's statement under oath is accepted regarding profit, loss, and destruction.

Core Idea
Partnership capital is a trust: the partner is liable only for transgression, and his word under oath is accepted.

After discussing the partner's authorities, the passage explains the legal status of the capital in his hands. It is a trust (amanah), not subject to liability for ordinary loss, akin to a deposit (wadi'ah) or loan for use (ariyah). The passage contrasts this with possession for exchange (buyer on approval) or security (pledgee). Because the capital is a trust, the partner's statement under oath is accepted regarding profit, loss, destruction, and payments to his co-partner. This lesson clarifies the legal definition of amanah and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling: Partner's Hand is Amanah
The text explicitly states 'wa yaduhu fi al-mal amanah' (his hand over the capital is a trust). This is the core ruling.
This is a legal classification, not a hukm taklifi (obligation).
2
Understand the Legal Basis for Amanah
The capital is a trust because the partner took possession with the owner's permission but not as part of an exchange (badal) or security (wathiqah). This distinguishes it from possession by a buyer on approval (sawm al-shira') or a pledgee (rahn).
The comparison highlights the absence of liability for the asset itself.
3
Contrast with Non-Amanah Possession
The text lists two counterexamples: (1) possession on approval (for exchange) is liable because it is taken with intent to buy; (2) possession as pledge (for security) is liable because the pledgee has a right to hold the asset as collateral. In both, the possessor guarantees the asset.
The key distinction is the nature of the permission: permission without obligation of substitution or security yields amanah.
4
Derive the Evidentiary Rule
Because the capital is a trust, the partner's statement under oath is accepted regarding the amount of profit, loss, destruction, and payment to the co-partner. This applies during his lifetime and after his death.
This is a procedural benefit: the trustee is not easily held liable.
5
Generalize to Similar Trustees
The same amanah rule applies to the mudarib (investment agent), wasi (executor), and mutawalli (administrator of waqf). Their possession is also with permission and not for exchange or security.
This creates a consistent category of fiduciaries in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
أمانة (amanah): In this context, the capital held by a partner is considered a trust, meaning he is not liable for loss except due to negligence or transgression.
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit: a contract where one party leaves property with another for safekeeping without compensation.
عارية (ariyah): A loan for use: a contract where one party allows another to use a property without compensation, with the obligation to return it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a partnership, if the capital is destroyed and the partner claims it was an accident, what is the evidentiary rule according to the Hanafi school?
A) The partner must provide two witnesses to avoid liability.
B) The partner's statement under oath is accepted, and he is not liable unless transgression is proven.
C) The loss is split equally between the partners.
D) The partner is automatically liable for loss of trust property.

Key Takeaway
Partnership capital is a trust (amanah), so the partner is not liable for loss without transgression, and his statement under oath is accepted as evidence.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
8 min
Partnership of Industries (Sharika al-Taqabbul): Validity by Istihsan
Discusses the validity and rules of partnership in accepting work without capital.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sharika al-taqabbul, explain the istihsan-based proof, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Profit need not require capital; partnership in work is valid by istihsan.

This passage deals with a partnership of craftsmen who pool their labor rather than capital. The Hanafi school upholds its validity through istihsan (juristic preference), despite the apparent qiyas (analogy) to capital-based partnerships. The text also addresses conditions of trade and place, profit-sharing, and the binding nature of contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the partnership type and its ruling
Understand what sharika al-taqabbul is: two or more craftsmen agree to accept work jointly without contributing capital. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sahih (valid) by istihsan.
This is the third type of partnership in Hanafi fiqh: partnership of industries.
2
Understand the opposing positions
Al-Shafi'i and Zufar (in one narration) hold it invalid because they argue profit requires capital (ra's al-mal). Malik and Zufar also condition unity of trade and place.
The opposing school relies on qiyas to capital partnerships.
3
Follow the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof: the objective is profit, which can be obtained through work as in mudaraba. Each partner appoints the other as agent, making each principal in half the work and agent in the other half, realizing partnership in profit.
The contract is a combination of agency (wakala) and partnership.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis enforce the partnership as binding (work accepted by one binds both, profit shared as agreed); under the opposing view, earnings would belong to the individual and the contract would be void.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the Hanafi view due to customary practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقبل: [ أي الثالث من أنواع شركة العقد شركة تقبل، وتسمى شركة الصنائع وشركة الأعمال أيضاً. (عيني) ] وتسمى شركة الأبدان أيضاً، وهي أن يشترك صانعان أن يتقبلا العمل، ويكون الكسب بينهما، سواء كانا متحدي العمل كالخياطين أو مختلفي العمل كخياط وصباغ بلا اختلاط ،مال وهي جائزة عندنا، وقال الشافعي وزفر في رواية: لا يجوز؛ لأن الشركة في الربح تبتني على الشركة في رأس المال، ولا مال لهما، فكيف يتصور الربح بدون الأصل؟ ولنا أن المقصود منهما إنما هو تحصيل الربح على الاشتراك، وهو لا يقتصر على المال بل يكون بالعمل أيضاً، فإذا وكل كل منهما الآخر بقبول العمل، كان كل واحد أصلاً في نصف العمل المتقبل، ووكيلاً في النصف الآخر، فتحقق الشركة في المال المستفاد وهو الربح، وهذا العقد مما يقبل التوكيل فيجوز. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني وصباغ أو نحوهما فلا يلزم اتحاد صنعة ومكان. ويكون الكسب بينهما أي أجر الكسب الذي يمكن استحقاقه كتعليم كتابة وقرآن وفقه على المفتى به، بخلاف شركة دلالين ومفتيين وشهود محاكم وقراء ووعاظ وسؤال؛ لأن التوكيل بالسؤال لا يصح، وكذا لواشتركا في عمل حرام لم يصح، وأما شركة الحمالين فصحيحة، فالأجر الذي يحصل من العمل يكون بين الشريكين مناصفة، ولو شرطا أكثر الربح لأدناهما عملا فالأصح الجواز، وكون الكسب بينهما يجوز استحساناً عندنا، وقال زفر ومالك: لا يجوز مع اختلاف الصنعة والمكان كالخياط والصباغ؛ لأن الشركة هي الخلطة، ولا خلطة فيها. ولنا: أن أول هذا العقد توكيل بالتصرف، وآخره اشتراك في الربح، فصار كالمضاربة، فلا يشترط اتحاد وكذا لا يشترط اتحاد المكان مثل أن يُجلس آخر على دكانه فيطرح عليه العمل بالنصف، والقياس أن - يلزمهما وكسب أحدهما بينهما. ووجوه: إن اشتركا بلا مال على أن يشتريا بوجوههما ويبيعا، وتتضمن الوكالة، أثلاثاً، أي بوجاهتهما عند الناس أي شركة الوجوه عند الإطلاق أداء - لا يجوز؛ لأن من أحدهما العمل ومن الآخر الحانوت واستحسن جوازها؛ لأن التقبل من صاحب الحانوت عمل. رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] (فتح) يلزمهما : [ أي يلزم الشريكين جميعا حتى يطالب كل منهما بالعمل ويطالب كل منهما بالأجرة، ويبرأ دافعها بالدفع إلى أحدهما. (ط)] أي العمل الذي يتقبله أحدهما يلزم شريكه حتى لو دفع رجل إلى أحدهما عملا فله أن يأخذ بذلك العمل أيهما شاء، ولكل واحد منهما أن يطالب بأجرة العمل وإلى أيهما دفع الأجرة برئ عن الأجرة؛ لأن كل ما يتقبله أحدهما مضمون على الآخر، فكان كالمفاوضة في ضمان الأعمال والمطالبة بالأبدان ويطالبان بالأجر، ر، ويبر آن بعمل أحدهما [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] (فتح) وكسب : يعني إذا عمل أحدهما دون الآخر، كانت الأجرة بينهما على ما شرطا ولو شرطا العمل نصفين والربح جاز استحساناً، وفي القياس لا يجوز؛ لأن الشركة وقعت مطلقة عن ذكر الكفالة والأحكام المذكورة من موجباتها، ويجوز اشتراط الربح بينهما على السواء وعلى التفاضل بأن يكون أحدهما أحذق من الآخر في العمل، وعند زفر: لا يجوز متفاضلاً. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] وعندنا يجوز؛ لأن الربح بقدر ضمان العمل لا بحقيقة العمل، فإن غاب أحدهما أو مرض ولم يعمل وعمل الآخر، فهو أيضاً بينهما. (فتح)
And acceptance [partnership]: [Meaning the third type of contract partnership: partnership of acceptance, also called partnership of industries and partnership of works. (Ayni)] It is also called partnership of bodies. It is that two craftsmen associate to accept work, and the earnings are between them, whether they are of the same trade like two tailors or different trades like a tailor and a dyer without mixing of capital. It is permissible according to us. Al-Shafi'i and Zufar in one narration say: it is not permissible because partnership in profit is built upon partnership in capital, and they have no capital, so how can profit be conceived without the original? And our proof is that their objective is only to obtain profit jointly, and that is not limited to capital but also through work. So when each appoints the other as agent for accepting work, each is a principal in half of the accepted work and an agent in the other half, so partnership in the acquired wealth (i.e., profit) is realized. This contract is one that accepts agency, so it is permissible. (Mukhtalaf, Fath, Ayni) And a dyer or the like – so unity of trade and place is not required. And the earnings are between them, meaning the wage of earnings that can be claimed, like teaching writing, Quran, and fiqh according to the fatwa, unlike partnership of brokers, muftis, court witnesses, reciters, preachers, and beggars because agency in begging is not valid. Similarly, if they associate in forbidden work, it is not valid. As for the partnership of porters, it is valid. So the wage obtained from work is between the two partners equally. If they stipulate more profit for the one who does less work, the correct view is permissibility. And that the earnings are between them is permitted by istihsan according to us. Zufar and Malik said: it is not permitted with difference of trade and place, like a tailor and a dyer, because partnership is mixing, and there is no mixing. And our proof is that the beginning of this contract is agency to transact, and its end is partnership in profit, so it becomes like mudaraba, so unity of trade is not required. Similarly, unity of place is not required, like one seating the other in his shop and assigning work to him for half. And by qiyas it would not be binding on them, but by istihsan it is. (Fath) It is binding on them: [Meaning it is binding on both partners such that each is demanded for work and each is demanded for the wage, and the one who pays is absolved by paying to either of them. (T)] That is, the work that one of them accepts is binding on his partner, so if a man gives work to one of them, he may demand either of them for that work, and each may demand the wage for the work, and whichever pays the wage is absolved because everything one accepts is guaranteed on the other, so it is like mufawada in guaranteeing works and demanding persons. They are both demanded for the wage, and they are absolved by the work of one of them. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 468/1] (Fath) And earnings: means if one works without the other, the wage is between them as they stipulated. If they stipulate half work and half profit, it is permitted by istihsan, but by qiyas it is not permitted because the partnership was concluded absolutely without mentioning guarantee and the mentioned rulings from its requisites. And it is permitted to stipulate profit equally or with disparity such that one is more skilled than the other in work. According to Zufar: it is not permitted with disparity. According to us, it is permitted because profit is in proportion to the guarantee of work, not the actual work. If one is absent or sick and does not work, and the other works, it is also between them. (Fath)
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of sharika al-taqabbul (partnership of industries/acceptance). The Hanafi school holds it permissible by istihsan, while al-Shafi'i and Zufar consider it invalid because partnership in profit requires partnership in capital. The Hanafi response is that the objective is joint profit, which can be achieved through work as well as capital; each partner appoints the other as agent to accept work, making each a principal in half the accepted work and an agent in the other half. Thus partnership is realized in the profit. The text then discusses conditions: the partners may be of different trades (e.g., tailor and dyer) and in different places; the earnings are the wages for permissible work like teaching, but not for impermissible activities like brokering or begging. The partnership of porters is valid. If they stipulate unequal profit shares for unequal work, it is permitted because profit correlates with the guarantee of work, not the actual labor. Zufar and Malik disallow disparity, but the Hanafis allow it by istihsan. The work accepted by one is binding on both; the customer may demand payment from either, and payment to one absolves the debtor. The text also clarifies that if one partner does all the work while the other is absent, the profit is still shared as agreed.

Key Terms
شركة التقبل (sharika al-taqabbul): A partnership where two or more craftsmen agree to accept work from customers and share the earnings, without contributing capital.
استحسان (istihsan): A legal preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a ruling that is more suitable, based on custom, necessity, or equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, may two craftsmen of different trades form a partnership to accept work and share profits?
A) No, because there is no mixing (khalta).
B) Yes, because each becomes agent and principal in the work.
C) No, because profits cannot be earned without capital.
D) Yes, but only if they work in the same place.

Key Takeaway
Sharika al-taqabbul is valid by istihsan; profit can arise from work, not just capital.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
12 min
Credit Partnership (Sharika al-Wujuh) – Validity Through Agency
Inter-madhhab dispute over credit partnership validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on sharika al-wujuh and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument regarding the necessity of capital.

Core Idea
Credit partnership is valid through mutual agency; profit does not require initial capital.

This lesson examines the credit partnership (sharika al-wujuh), where two parties with creditworthiness but no capital buy goods on credit and share profits. The Hanafi school permits it based on agency, while al-Shafi'i and Malik reject it because profit is tied to capital. We will explore the competing proofs and the practical difference in enforceability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
Define sharika al-wujuh: a partnership where partners contribute creditworthiness, not capital, to buy and sell on credit and share profits. Note its alternative names (partnership of the destitute) and the Hanafi premise that it is permissible.
The text clarifies that it is the fourth type of contract partnership.
2
State the Hanafi position and proof
State that the Hanafi school holds it sahih (valid). Their proof: the purpose of partnership (profit) is achieved through agency (wakala), and buying/selling are valid subjects of agency. Each partner is an agent of the other.
The text uses 'li-anna al-maqsuda min al-sharika tahsil al-ribh bi-al-wakala'.
3
State the opposing school's position and proof
Al-Shafi'i and Malik hold it invalid. Their proof: profit is a branch (far') of capital; without capital, no profit can arise, and agency alone cannot create a partnership in profit.
The text quotes 'al-ribh far' al-mal, fala tanaqid badunihi'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that profit can arise from trade even without initial capital, as credit purchases and sales generate profit. The mutual agency creates a valid basis for the partnership, and no authority exists otherwise.
The text adds that acting for another requires agency or authority; authority is absent, so agency is necessary.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under Hanafi law, such partnerships are enforceable and can be structured as 'inan or mufawada. Under Shafi'i/Maliki law, the arrangement is void; the parties would be treated as independent buyers/sellers.
The text explains that if they stipulate mufawada and its conditions, it becomes mufawada; otherwise 'inan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوه [ أي الرابع من أنواع شركة العقد شركة وجوه. (عيني) ] وتسمى أيضاً شركة المفاليس وسميت بها؛ لأنه لا يشتري بالنسيئة إلا من له وجاهة عند الناس، وقيل؛ لأنهما يشتريان من الوجه الذي لا يعرف، وقيل: لأنهما إذا جلسا ليدبرا أمرهما ينظر كل واحد منهما إلى وجه صاحبه رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] وقيل: إنما أضيفت للوجوه؛ لأنها تبتذل معها لعدم المال، وهذه الشركة جائزة عندنا وقال الشافعي ومالك: لا تجوز؛ لأن الربح فرع المال، فلا تنعقد ،بدونه ولنا أن المقصود من الشركة تحصيل الربح بالوكالة والبيع والشراء مما يقبل الوكالة، فيكون كل واحد منهما وكيلاً عن الآخر فيما يشتريه؛ لأنه لا ولاية له على صاحبه إلا به. ثم هذه الشركة تكون عناناً ومفاوضة كشركة التقبل، فإذا نصا على المفاوضة وذكرا جميع ما تقتضيه المفاوضة، واجتمعت فيها شرائطها صارت مفاوضة وإلا فعنان وقوله تتضمن الوكالة؛ لأنه بذلك يتمكن من التحصيل لصاحبه؛ إذ لا ولاية له عليه وتتضمن الكفالة أيضاً مع ذلك إذا كانت مفاوضة، فكل واحد منهما وكيل الآخر فيما يشتري به؛ لأن التصرف على الغير لا يجوز إلا بوكالة أو ولاية له، ولا ولاية، فتعينت الوكالة. (مستخلص، فتح) ويبيعا فما حصل بالبيع يدفعان منه ثمن ما اشترياه بالنسيئة وما بقي بينهما. (ط) الوكالة فتكون عناناً، وتكون مفاوضة إذا تضمنت الكفالة بشرطها السابق. (ط)
Faces [Meaning the fourth type of contract partnership: partnership of faces. (Ayni)] It is also called partnership of the destitute, and it is called that because only one who has creditworthiness (wajaha) among people can buy on credit. And it is said: because they buy from a face (source) that is unknown. And it is said: because when they sit to deliberate their affairs, each looks at the face of his companion. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 468/1] And it is said: it is attributed to faces because they are exposed due to lack of capital. This partnership is permissible according to us. Al-Shafi'i and Malik said: it is not permissible because profit is a branch of capital, so it cannot be concluded without it. And our proof is that the purpose of partnership is to obtain profit through agency, and buying and selling are subject to agency. So each of them is an agent for the other in what he buys, because he has no authority over his companion except through that. Then this partnership can be 'inan or mufawada like the partnership of acceptance. So if they stipulate mufawada and mention all that mufawada requires, and its conditions are met, it becomes mufawada; otherwise it is 'inan. And his statement (that it includes agency) is because thereby he is able to acquire for his companion, as he has no authority over him. And it also includes guarantee (kafala) when it is mufawada. So each is an agent of the other in what he buys, because acting on behalf of another is not permissible except by agency or authority, and there is no authority, so agency is determined. (Mukhtalaf, Fath) And they sell; then from the sale proceeds they pay the price of what they bought on credit, and the remainder is between them. (T) Agency: so it becomes 'inan, and it becomes mufawada when it includes guarantee with its previous condition. (T)
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding sharika al-wujuh (credit partnership). The Hanafi school holds it permissible, while al-Shafi'i and Malik deem it invalid because profit derives from capital, not from mere creditworthiness. The Hanafi response is that the purpose of partnership is profit through agency, and buying/selling are valid agency transactions; each partner acts as agent for the other. The partnership can be either 'inan (limited) or mufawada (full) depending on the inclusion of guarantee (kafala). If they stipulate all conditions of mufawada, it becomes mufawada; otherwise it is 'inan. The text also explains that agency is necessary because no one has inherent authority over another. In practice, they buy goods on credit, sell them, pay the debt, and share the profit.

Key Terms
شركة وجوه (sharika al-wujuh): A partnership where two or more persons with creditworthiness buy goods on credit with the agreement to sell and share profits, without contributing capital.
مفاوضة (mufawada): A full partnership where partners are equal in all aspects, including agency and guarantee, with full delegation of authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary basis for the validity of sharika al-wujuh?
A) The existence of capital contributed by both partners.
B) The creditworthiness of the partners and their mutual agency.
C) The presence of a written contract.
D) The equal division of profits.

Key Takeaway
Sharika al-wujuh is valid in Hanafi law because the purpose of partnership (profit) can be achieved through mutual agency and credit purchases, without capital.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
6 min
Partnership of Credit: Hanafi Validity and the Dispute with Shafi‘i and Maliki
Definition, validity, and legal effects of credit-based partnership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates shirkat al-wujuh and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i and Maliki argument.

Core Idea
A partnership without capital is valid because profit follows the guarantee of work, not ownership of capital.

Shirkat al-wujuh, or partnership of credit, is a unique Hanafi contract where partners rely on their reputations to buy and sell on credit. This lesson explores its definition, the inter-madhhab dispute over its validity, and its legal effects. You will learn the Hanafi justification based on agency and the counterarguments of Shafi‘i and Maliki scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State that shirkat al-wujuh is permissible (ja'iz) according to Abu Hanifa and his students.
2
State the opposing view
Shafi‘i and Malik consider it invalid because profit is derived from capital.
3
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
The purpose of partnership is profit through agency and trade, which can exist without capital.
4
Examine the qiyas vs istihsan
The text notes that by qiyas it would be invalid, but istihsan permits it based on the value of agency and guarantee.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, such partnerships are valid; under Shafi'i/Maliki, they are not, affecting business structuring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة
٢٣٦
أحكام الشركة
يلزمهما وكسب أحدهما بينهما.
ووجوه: إن اشتركا بلا مال على أن يشتريا بوجوههما ويبيعا، وتتضمن الوكالة،
أثلاثاً،
أي بوجاهتهما عند
الناس أي شركة الوجوه عند الإطلاق
أداء
- لا يجوز؛ لأن من أحدهما العمل ومن الآخر الحانوت واستحسن جوازها؛ لأن التقبل من صاحب الحانوت عمل. رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] (فتح) يلزمهما : [ أي يلزم الشريكين جميعا حتى يطالب كل منهما بالعمل ويطالب كل منهما بالأجرة، ويبرأ دافعها بالدفع إلى أحدهما. (ط)] أي العمل الذي يتقبله أحدهما يلزم شريكه حتى لو دفع رجل إلى أحدهما عملا فله أن يأخذ بذلك العمل أيهما شاء، ولكل واحد منهما أن يطالب بأجرة العمل وإلى أيهما دفع الأجرة برئ عن الأجرة؛ لأن كل ما يتقبله أحدهما مضمون على الآخر، فكان كالمفاوضة في ضمان الأعمال والمطالبة بالأبدان ويطالبان بالأجر، ر، ويبر آن بعمل أحدهما [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] (فتح) وكسب : يعني إذا عمل أحدهما دون الآخر، كانت الأجرة بينهما على ما شرطا ولو شرطا العمل نصفين والربح جاز استحساناً، وفي القياس لا يجوز؛ لأن الشركة وقعت مطلقة عن ذكر الكفالة والأحكام المذكورة من موجباتها، ويجوز اشتراط الربح بينهما على السواء وعلى التفاضل بأن يكون أحدهما أحذق من الآخر في العمل، وعند زفر: لا يجوز متفاضلاً. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٨/١] وعندنا يجوز؛ لأن الربح بقدر ضمان العمل لا بحقيقة العمل، فإن غاب أحدهما أو مرض ولم يعمل وعمل الآخر، فهو أيضاً بينهما. (فتح) وجوه [ أي الرابع من أنواع شركة العقد شركة وجوه. (عيني) ] وتسمى أيضاً شركة المفاليس وسميت بها؛ لأنه لا يشتري بالنسيئة إلا من له وجاهة عند الناس، وقيل؛ لأنهما يشتريان من الوجه الذي لا يعرف، وقيل: لأنهما إذا جلسا ليدبرا أمرهما ينظر كل واحد منهما إلى وجه صاحبه رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٩/١] وقيل: إنما أضيفت للوجوه؛ لأنها تبتذل معها لعدم المال، وهذه الشركة جائزة عندنا وقال الشافعي ومالك: لا تجوز؛ لأن الربح فرع المال، فلا تنعقد ،بدونه ولنا أن المقصود من الشركة تحصيل الربح بالوكالة والبيع والشراء مما يقبل الوكالة، فيكون كل واحد منهما وكيلاً عن الآخر فيما يشتريه؛ لأنه لا ولاية له على صاحبه إلا به.
ثم هذه الشركة تكون عناناً ومفاوضة كشركة التقبل، فإذا نصا على المفاوضة وذكرا جميع ما تقتضيه المفاوضة، واجتمعت فيها شرائطها صارت مفاوضة وإلا فعنان وقوله تتضمن الوكالة؛ لأنه بذلك يتمكن من التحصيل لصاحبه؛ إذ لا ولاية له عليه وتتضمن الكفالة أيضاً مع ذلك إذا كانت مفاوضة، فكل واحد منهما وكيل الآخر فيما يشتري به؛ لأن التصرف على الغير لا يجوز إلا بوكالة أو ولاية له، ولا ولاية، فتعينت الوكالة. (مستخلص، فتح) ويبيعا فما حصل بالبيع يدفعان منه ثمن ما اشترياه بالنسيئة وما بقي بينهما. (ط)
الوكالة فتكون عناناً، وتكون مفاوضة إذا تضمنت الكفالة بشرطها السابق. (ط)

فإن شرطا مناصفة المشترى أو مثالثته، فالرّبحُ كذلك، وبطل شرط الفضل.
أي الشريكان شركة الوجوه
Book of Partnership. Rulings of Partnership: It is binding on both, and the earnings of one are between them. And types: If they partner without capital, on condition that they buy with their credit and sell, and it includes agency, in thirds, i.e., with their standing among people, i.e., partnership of credit at absolute. Performance: It is not permissible, because one provides work and the other the shop, and its permissibility is approved by istihsan because acceptance from the shop owner is work. (Fath) 'It is binding on both': i.e., it binds both partners so that each is demanded for work and each is demanded for wages, and the payer is discharged by paying to one of them. (T) i.e., the work accepted by one binds his partner, so if a man gives work to one of them, he may take that work from whichever he wishes, and each has the right to demand the wage for the work, and to whichever he pays the wage, he is discharged from the wage because everything accepted by one is guaranteed by the other, so it is like a cooperative (mufawada) in guarantee of works and demand of persons, and they both demand the wage, and they are discharged by the work of one. (Fath) 'And earnings': means if one works without the other, the wage is between them according to their stipulation; even if they stipulate work in halves and the profit, it is permissible by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not permissible because the partnership was launched absolute without mention of guarantee, and the mentioned rulings are from its requirements. It is permissible to stipulate profit between them equally or by preference such that one is more skilled than the other in work. According to Zufar: it is not permissible with preference. According to us, it is permissible because profit is in proportion to the guarantee of work, not the reality of work. If one is absent or sick and does not work and the other works, it is also between them. (Fath) 'Wujuh': i.e., the fourth type of contractual partnership is partnership of credit. It is also called partnership of the penniless; it is named thus because only those with credit among people can buy on credit, and it is said because they buy from the face that is not known, and it is said because when they sit to manage their affairs, each looks at the face of his partner. It is said that it is attributed to faces because faces are exposed due to lack of capital. This partnership is permissible according to us, and al-Shafi'i and Malik said: it is not permissible because profit is a branch of capital, so it cannot be concluded without it. Our proof: the purpose of partnership is to earn profit through agency and buying and selling, which can accept agency, so each is an agent for the other in what he buys because he has no authority over his partner except through that. Then this partnership is 'inan and mufawada like partnership of acceptance. So if they stipulate mufawada and mention all that mufawada requires, and its conditions are met, it becomes mufawada; otherwise it is 'inan. And his statement 'it includes agency' because by that he is able to earn for his partner since he has no authority over him. It also includes guarantee with that if it is mufawada, so each is an agent for the other in what he buys because dealing for another is not permissible except by agency or authority, and there is no authority, so agency is determined. (Mukhtasar, Fath) 'And they sell': so what is obtained from the sale, they pay from it the price of what they bought on credit, and what remains is between them. (T) Agency, so it is 'inan, and it becomes mufawada if it includes guarantee with its previous condition. (T). Then if they stipulate half of the purchased item or a third, the profit is likewise, and the stipulation of excess is void. i.e., the two partners in partnership of credit.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the validity of shirkat al-wujuh (partnership of credit). The Hanafi school (followed by the author) holds it as permissible (ja'iz), while al-Shafi'i and Malik consider it invalid because profit is derived from capital, and here there is no capital. The Hanafi response argues that the essence of partnership is to earn profit through agency (wakala) and trade, which can exist without capital. The passage also details the legal effects: each partner is bound by the other's acceptance of work, wages are shared, and profit can be stipulated equally or by preference. It distinguishes between 'inan (limited) and mufawada (unlimited) forms. Additionally, if partners stipulate a share of the purchased item rather than profit, the profit follows ownership, and any stipulation of excess profit is void.

Key Terms
شركة الوجوه (shirkat al-wujuh): A partnership where partners contribute no capital but buy and sell on credit based on their reputation, with profit sharing as agreed.
مفاوضة (mufawada): An unlimited partnership where each partner is both agent and guarantor for the other, with full authority.
عنان ('inan): A limited partnership where each partner is only an agent, not a guarantor, and authority is restricted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In shirkat al-wujuh, what is the basis for profit distribution according to the Hanafi school?
A) The amount of capital contributed
B) The guarantee of work, not the actual work done
C) Equality regardless of work
D) The amount of time spent working

Key Takeaway
Shirkat al-wujuh is valid in Hanafi law because profit follows the guarantee of work through agency, not capital ownership.

Shirkah — Partnership

Invalid Partnership in Mubahat (Ownerless Items)
Ruling on partnerships for gathering free natural resources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partnerships in mubahat and explain why it is invalid using the analogy of agency.

Core Idea
Partnership in mubahat is invalid because it implies agency over what the principal does not own.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses partnerships for collecting ownerless items like firewood, hunting, and water. While such agreements may seem practical, Hanafi law declares them invalid due to a fundamental principle: partnership includes agency (wakala), and agency over ownerless property is impossible. Understanding this ruling clarifies how ownership is established in mubah items and prevents disputes over earnings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the ruling
The passage specifically mentions three activities: ihtitab (woodcutting), istiyad (hunting), and istiqa' (drawing water). These are all examples of mubah (ownerless) items. The ruling is that a partnership (shirkah) in these activities is not valid (la tasihh).
The section title explicitly calls this 'al-shirkah al-fasidah' (the invalid partnership).
2
Analyze the reasoning: partnership implies agency
The text explains that a partnership contract inherently includes an element of agency (wakala). Agency requires that the principal own the property or have legal authority over it. Since mubah items are not owned until they are physically taken (istila'), the principal cannot authorize another to acquire them on his behalf.
The key phrase: 'لأن الشركة متضمنة معنى الوكالة' — partnership implies the meaning of agency.
3
Apply the qiyas: agency over mubah is invalid, so partnership is invalid
The original case (asl) is agency over mubah: it is invalid because the principal does not own the item. The new case (far') is partnership in mubah. The effective cause (illa) is the inclusion of agency. Therefore, by analogy (qiyas), the partnership is also invalid.
This qiyas is of type jaliyyah (clear analogy) as the illa is explicitly stated.
4
Note the exceptions and ikhtilaf
The text notes that some scholars (Malik, Ahmad, and some Shafi'is) consider such partnerships valid. In Hanafi law, if one partner merely assists the other (e.g., carrying the wood), the assistant is entitled to wages (ujrat al-mithl) according to Muhammad, but the partnership itself remains invalid.
The difference between a valid partnership and mere assistance is crucial for practical outcomes.

Section: On the invalid partnership. And a partnership is not valid in woodcutting, hunting, and drawing water, and the earnings are for the worker, specifically due to the invalidity of the partnership. The purchased item with fatha on the ra' means that it is half between them. Or its division into thirds, i.e., that they stipulate a third of the purchased item so that it is between them in thirds: one third for one and two thirds for the other. And the stipulation of excess in profit is void, so the profit is between them according to ownership. Because profit is not deserved except through work like the mudarib, or through capital like the owner of capital, or through guarantee like the master who accepts work from people and delegates it to the student for less than he took, so the excess is permissible due to guarantee. And profit is not deserved otherwise. And guarantee is according to ownership in the purchased item, so the profit in excess of that is not guaranteed, so no profit is permissible if the purchased item is half between them and the profit is in thirds; rather, the profit is between them according to ownership. And excess is permissible in mudaraba contrary to analogy due to the specificity of capital. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 4/254) (Ayni, Fath). Section: On the invalid partnership. Ramiiz al-Haqa'iq 469: A partnership is not valid etc. because agency establishes the authority of disposition over what is established for the principal, and this meaning cannot be realized here because the principal does not own it, so he cannot deputize another in his place, and because mubah belongs to whoever takes it, so a ruling cannot be made for another. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 4/255). Similarly, partnership is not valid in all mubah items because partnership implies agency, and agency in taking mubah is void, so likewise partnership in it. Hunting, because hunting is mubah except for amusement, and taking it up as a profession is mubah in reality because it is a type of earning, and all types of earning are equal in permissibility according to the correct view. 'In taking' and 'water drawing': i.e., drawing water. Similarly, in gathering firewood and picking fruits from mountains, and likewise in every mubah, except according to Malik and Ahmad it is valid, and according to some Shafi'is: water drawing from mubah is valid. Similarly, it is not permissible if they partner in seeking treasures from mines, transporting clay from land they do not own, or gypsum, salt, kohl, or similar. Similarly, if they partner on making bricks from unowned clay or baking bricks, and similarly begging (soliciting from people) if they partner in it. (Ramiiz al-Haqa'iq 1/469) (Fath) 'Woodcutting': that two partner to cut wood from mountains and sell. (Ayni) 'And the earnings': i.e., the acquired from this partnership is for the worker etc., i.e., if the partnership in woodcutting and other mubah items is not valid, then what one acquires without the other's assistance is for the worker alone due to the cause, which is appropriation. If they both take together, it is half between them due to equality in appropriation. If one cuts wood and the other assists him, like one uproots and the other collects, or one hunts and the other carries, then the assistant has the equivalent of his wage, whatever it may be, according to Muhammad.

Commentary
This is a section on invalid partnerships (shirkah fasidah). The passage rules that partnerships in collecting mubah (ownerless) items like firewood, hunting, and drawing water are invalid because agency (wakala) cannot be established over something the principal does not own. The Hanafi school holds that such partnerships do not create shared ownership; rather, each person's earnings belong to him individually. There is a noted ikhtilaf: Malik and Ahmad consider such partnerships valid, and some Shafi'is also allow it for water-drawing. The passage also details that if one assists the other, the assistant is entitled to wages (ujrat al-mithl). The ruling extends to similar activities like digging for treasures, mining, making bricks from unowned clay, and even begging. The underlying reason is that partnership implies mutual agency, and agency in acquiring ownerless things is null.

Key Terms
احتطاب (ihtitab): Gathering firewood from mountains or forests for sale.
اصطياد (istiyad): Hunting wild animals (which are mubah).
استقاء (istiqa'): Drawing water from a well or source that is mubah (ownerless water).
وكالة (wakala): Agency: legal authority to act on behalf of another.
استيلاء (istila'): Physical appropriation or taking possession of an ownerless item, which establishes ownership.

Partnership in mubah (ownerless) items is invalid in Hanafi law because it involves agency over what the principal does not own, and earnings belong to the individual acquirer.

Profit in Voidable Partnership Follows Capital
Ruling on profit distribution in voidable partnership with invalid stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit distribution in a voidable partnership and apply the principle that profit must correspond to capital share.

Core Idea
In voidable partnership, profit follows ownership — any stipulation to the contrary is void.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common scenario: two partners contribute equal capital but agree to split profits unequally. The Hanafi school rules that such a stipulation is invalid, and profit must be divided according to the proportion of capital ownership. The reasoning is rooted in the principle that profit is earned through capital, work, or guarantee; since guarantee corresponds to ownership, profit cannot exceed that.

Guided Path
1
Identify the partnership type and its ruling
The passage discusses 'al-shirkah al-fasidah' (voidable partnership). Determine that it is fasid due to an invalid condition, but the contract itself can be corrected by removing the condition.
Fasid means voidable, not void; the contract is still effective in some respects.
2
Identify the invalid stipulation
The partners stipulated that the purchased goods would be owned equally (or in thirds) but that profit would be divided differently. This is a stipulation of surplus profit beyond ownership share.
In a valid partnership, profit must be proportional to capital; any deviation makes the partnership fasid.
3
Apply the principle that profit follows ownership
The ruling states that profit must be distributed according to the ownership ratio of the purchased goods. Since capital is equal, ownership is equal, so profit must be equal. The invalid stipulation is discarded.
The commentary gives the rationale: profit is earned through capital, work, or guarantee. Guarantee corresponds to ownership, so surplus profit without guarantee is not permissible.
4
Contrast with mudarabah
In mudarabah, profit can be stipulated unequally because the capital is specified and the mudarib only contributes work. This is an exception to the general rule, based on necessity.
The passage explicitly mentions that mudarabah is 'contrary to analogy' due to the specificity of capital.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشركة ۲۳۷ الشركة الفاسدة فإن شرطا مناصفة المشترى أو مثالثته، فالرّبحُ كذلك، وبطل شرط الفضل. أي الشريكان شركة الوجوه أي كما شرطا في المشترى المشترى بفتح الراء يعني أن يكون بينهما نصفين. أو مثالثته أي أو شرطا مثالثة المشترى بأن يكون بينهما أثلاثاً: الثلث لأحدهما والثلثان للآخر. وبطل شرط الفضل في الربح فيكون الربح بينهما بقدر الملك. [لأن الربح لا يستحق إلا بالعمل كالمضارب، أو بالمال كرب المال، أو بالضمان كالأستاذ الذي يتقبل العمل من الناس، ويلقيه على التلميذ بأقل مما أخذ فيطيب له الفضل بالضمان، ولا يستحق الربح بغير هذه الأشياء، والضمان بقدر الملك في المشترى، فكان الربح الزائد عليه ما لم يضمن فلا ربح يجوز أن يكون المشترى بينهما نصفين والربح أثلاثاً بل يكون الربح بينهما بقدر الملك، ويجوز الفضل في المضاربة على خلاف القياس؛ لتعين المال فيها. تبيين الحقائق: ٢٥٤/٤] (عيني، فتح)
The voidable partnership: If they stipulate equal ownership of the purchased item or its division into thirds, the profit is likewise, and the stipulation of surplus is void. That is, the two partners in a partnership of credit. The purchased item with fath on the ra means that it is half each. Or its division into thirds: they stipulate dividing the purchased item into thirds, so that one gets one third and the other gets two thirds. The stipulation of surplus in profit is void, so profit is between them according to ownership. [Because profit is not earned except through work like the mudarib, or through capital like the owner of capital, or through guarantee like the master who accepts work from people and assigns it to the apprentice for less than what he took, so the surplus is permissible for him due to guarantee. Profit is not earned through other than these things. Guarantee is according to ownership in the purchased item. Thus, if the surplus profit is what he did not guarantee, then it is not permissible for the purchased item to be between them half and the profit a third; rather, profit is between them according to ownership. The surplus is permissible in mudarabah contrary to analogy because the capital is specified. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 4:254] (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on voidable partnership (shirkah fasidah). It states that if partners stipulate that the purchased goods will be owned equally (half each) or in thirds (one third and two thirds), then the profit distribution must follow that ownership ratio. Any stipulation giving one partner more profit than his ownership share is void. The commentary explains that profit is only earned through one of three means: work (like a mudarib), capital (like a rabb al-mal), or guarantee (like a master who guarantees the work). Since guarantee corresponds to ownership in the purchased item, profit cannot exceed ownership share. This is unlike mudarabah where surplus profit can be stipulated because the capital is specified (the mudarib works while the rabb al-mal provides capital). In voidable partnership, invalid stipulations are discarded, and profit is divided according to capital contribution.

Key Terms
الشركة الفاسدة (al-shirkah al-fasidah): A voidable partnership where an invalid condition is present but the contract may be corrected by removing the condition.
مناصفة (munasafah): Dividing into two equal halves.
مثالثة (muthalathah): Dividing into three parts, with shares of one third and two thirds.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; liability for loss. In this context, it refers to the risk borne by the partner proportional to ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 70-30 as stipulated
B) 50-50
C) The partnership is void, so no profit is distributed
D) Only the partner who worked more gets profit

Key Takeaway
In voidable partnership, profit is distributed according to capital share; any contrary stipulation is invalid and discarded.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate

Invalid Partnerships: Rulings on Mubah and Profit Distribution
Explains which activities cannot form a valid partnership and the distribution of earnings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which types of partnerships are invalid in the Hanafi school, explain the legal reasoning based on agency, and apply the rules for profit distribution and compensation in voidable partnerships.

Core Idea
A partnership in ownerless property is invalid—profit follows capital, not stipulation.

This passage tackles a key distinction in Hanafi partnership law: partnerships based on collecting ownerless (mubah) items such as firewood, game, or water are voidable. The reason lies in the nature of agency—one cannot appoint another over something one does not own. The text then navigates the consequences: how earnings are divided, how profit is allocated, and an internal Hanafi difference on compensation. Understanding this helps you see how form and substance interact in Islamic commercial law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalid partnerships
List the activities that cannot form a valid partnership according to the passage. These include ihtitab (firewood collection), istiyad (hunting), istiqa' (drawing water), and similar acts involving mubah property.
All involve ownerless items taken from nature.
2
Understand the legal rationale
The invalidity stems from the fact that partnership implies agency (wakalah), and agency cannot be established over something the principal does not own. Since mubah becomes owned only by the one who takes it, the partner cannot delegate authority to the other.
This is a pure Hanafi usul argument.
3
Determine earnings distribution when the partnership is void
If only one partner works, he keeps all earnings. If both work equally, earnings are split equally. If one works and the other assists, the assistant is entitled to fair wages (ajr mithl).
Focus on the scenario of assistance: full fair wages according to Muhammad, half according to Abu Yusuf.
4
Apply the rule on profit distribution
In voidable partnerships, profit is proportional to capital contribution, regardless of what the partners stipulated. Any stipulation of extra profit is void. This is harmonized with the earlier earnings rule by distinguishing between partnerships in mubah (earnings based on work) and partnerships with capital (profit based on capital).
This resolves the apparent contradiction in the author's statements.
5
Recognize other rulings: termination and zakat
The partnership is terminated by death (including legal death like apostasy). One partner may not pay zakat on the other's wealth without permission, as zakat is not part of trade activities covered by the partnership.
These are subsidiary but important practical rules.

Chapter on explaining the voidable partnership. It is not valid for a partnership in collecting firewood, hunting, and drawing water, and the earnings are for the worker. Because agency is the establishment of authority to dispose of something that is established for the principal, and this meaning cannot be realized here because the principal does not own it, so he cannot appoint another in his place. And because the permissible (mubah) belongs to whoever takes it, so it is not possible to place a ruling on it for someone else. Likewise, partnership is not valid for all other permissible things because partnership includes the meaning of agency, and it is invalid in taking permissible things, so too the partnership therein. Hunting because the game is permissible except for amusement; taking it as a trade is permissible according to the correct view because it is a type of earning and all types of earning are equal in permissibility on the correct view. And drawing water: i.e., extracting water. Likewise in gathering firewood and collecting fruits from mountains, and likewise in every permissible thing except according to Malik and Ahmad it is valid, and according to some Shafi'is it is valid: drawing water from a permissible source. Likewise, it is not permissible if they partner in seeking treasures from mines, transporting clay from land they do not own, or gypsum, salt, antimony, or the like. Likewise, if they partner to make bricks from non-owned clay or bake bricks. Likewise, begging (asking people) is not permissible if they partner in it. Collecting firewood: that two people agree to collect firewood from mountains and sell it. And the earnings: i.e., what is earned from this partnership. If the partnership in collecting firewood and other permissible things is not valid, then what one acquires without the assistance of the other is for the worker exclusively because the cause (taking possession) is from him. If they both take it together, it is half each due to equality in possession. If one collects firewood and the other assists him by one uprooting and the other gathering, or one catches the game and the other carries it, then the assistant is entitled to his full fair wages according to Muhammad, and he owes fair wages to the other. Profit in voidable partnership is according to capital even if they stipulate surplus. The partnership is terminated by the death of one of them, even if legally (by apostasy). One may not pay zakat on the other's wealth without permission. According to Abu Yusuf: It (the compensation) should not exceed half its value. Likewise, if they partner in drawing water, one having a mule and the other a water-skin to draw water on it, whichever draws water gets the wages and owes the fair wages of the water-skin or mule. Fair wages are obligatory because he has benefited from another's property through a void contract, so he owes fair wages. The correct view is that the voidable partnership which can be made valid is a partnership according to capital. It should not be said that the author's words are contradictory because he first mentioned that earnings in voidable partnership are for the worker and he owes fair wages to the other, then he said the opposite with his statement 'profit in voidable partnership is according to capital even if they stipulate surplus'. Because the first case concerns partnership in drawing water from a river, while the second concerns partnership in buying and selling a well, where they stipulated profit in thirds with equal capital but a defect occurred due to an extraneous reason like stipulating one partner a specific amount of dirhams from the profit. He indicated by his statement 'even if they stipulate surplus' that the permissibility of stipulating surplus in profit with equal capital applies when the partnership is valid; when it is void, it does not, and profit is according to capital. If the capital is from one partner only, the other gets fair wages. Profit is dependent on the contract when it exists; here the contract is absent so it depends on capital. The increase is due to stipulation, but it was invalidated by the void contract, so it is as if no stipulation existed. Thus, the stipulation of surplus is void and entitlement remains according to capital. The partnership is terminated absolutely, whether the partner knows of the death or not, because partnership includes agency, and agency ends with death as it is a legal removal. Thus, if agency becomes void, so does partnership. This is unlike if the partner dissolves the partnership when he has the right to dissolve, as when the capital is dirhams and dinars, which depends on the other's knowledge because it is an intentional removal. Legally: that is, if the death is legal (by apostasy and joining the enemy territory and a judgment of his joining), if no judgment is passed, the partnership is suspended by consensus; if he returns before the judgment, it remains; if he dies or is killed, it is terminated. Regarding whether it becomes an 'inan partnership during suspension? The Imam (Abu Hanifa) denied it, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) affirmed it. He may not pay zakat: that is, one partner may not pay zakat on the other's wealth without permission because paying zakat is not part of trade activities, so it is not included in the partnership; permission is required. If he pays without permission, it is not fulfilled on behalf of the owner, but is a donation from the payer. Without permission: because permission in trade and zakat is not from it.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a chapter (fasl) on explaining voidable partnership. It first addresses partnerships involving the collection of ownerless (mubah) items like firewood, hunting, and drawing water. Such partnerships are invalid because agency cannot be established over ownerless property—each person owns only what he personally takes. The commentary notes that according to Malik, Ahmad, and some Shafi'is such partnerships are valid, but the Hanafi position is that they are not. Next, the passage details earnings in voidable partnerships: if one partner works alone, he keeps all earnings; if both work, it is divided equally; if one assists the other, the assistant is entitled to fair wages (ajr mithl). On the amount of compensation, Imam Muhammad says the assistant gets full fair wages, while Abu Yusuf limits it to half the value—the correct view is Muhammad's. Then the passage discusses profit distribution: in a voidable partnership, profit follows capital proportion, not any stipulated surplus. This is harmonized with the earlier statement about earnings: earnings from working with mubah are for the worker, but if the partnership involves capital (e.g., buying a well), profit follows capital. The partnership is terminated by death, even legal death like apostasy. Finally, a partner may not pay zakat on another partner's wealth without explicit permission, as paying zakat is not within the scope of trade activities.

Key Terms
احتطاب (ihtitab): Collecting firewood from mountains or forests.
اصطياد (istiyad): Hunting animals for trade or consumption.
استقاء (istiqa'): Drawing water from a well, river, or other source.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Fair market wage for the work or use of property.
الشركة الفاسدة (al-shirkah al-fasidah): A partnership that is flawed due to an invalid condition but may be corrected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if two people enter a voidable partnership to collect firewood, and only one person actually collects the wood while the other merely carries it, how is the earnings distributed?
A) The collector keeps all earnings because he did the work.
B) The collector must give half the earnings to the carrier.
C) The collector keeps the earnings but must pay the carrier fair wages.
D) The earnings are divided equally because they agreed to share.

Key Takeaway
Partnerships in ownerless property are voidable; earnings follow possession or capital, not stipulation, and fair wages are owed for assistance.

Shirkah — Partnership
intermediate
12 min
Profit in a Defective Partnership Follows Capital
Ruling with proof on profit in fasid shirkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit distribution in a fasid shirkah and explain the distinction between service and capital partnerships.

Core Idea
In a defective partnership, any stipulated condition for excess profit is void; profit is distributed according to capital.

This passage resolves an apparent contradiction: earlier it says the worker gets earnings and owes hire-mithl to the other partner, but later it says profit follows capital. The key is the type of partnership: service partnerships (e.g., drawing water with assets) vs. capital partnerships (e.g., buying and selling). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the ruling on defective partnerships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two distinct situations: (1) a service partnership where one provides labor and the other provides an asset (mule/water-skin), and (2) a capital partnership where both contribute money for trade. The rulings differ in each case.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
In the service partnership, the worker gets the earnings and must pay the asset owner a hire-mithl (fair hire) for the use of the asset. In the capital partnership, profit is distributed according to the capital contributed, and any condition for excess profit is void.
The text explicitly says: 'the profit in a defective partnership is according to the capital even if a surplus was stipulated.'
3
Understand the proof (ta'lil)
The reasoning is: profit follows the contract; but if the contract is defective (fasid), the contract is as if non-existent, so profit follows capital. The stipulated condition for excess profit is tied to a defective contract, so it is void.
The text states: 'profit follows the contract when it exists, but here the contract is absent, so it follows the capital.'
4
Apply the ruling to the example
In the example of drawing water: one has a mule, the other a water-skin. Whoever performs the labor gets the hire for that labor, but must pay the other the fair hire for the use of his asset. This illustrates the principle for service partnerships.
The hire-mithl is wajib because the benefit was utilized through a defective contract.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the hire-mithl cannot exceed half the value of the asset's benefit, while Imam Abu Hanifa says the full hire-mithl must be paid. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's.
This is mentioned in the commentary: 'According to Abu Yusuf: he does not exceed half its value.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
